   - `PassInfoMixin<DerivedT>` at line 70: CRTP mixin providing `name()` and `printPipeline()`
   - `AnalysisInfoMixin<DerivedT>` at line 93: CRTP mixin for analyses, provides `ID()` returning `&DerivedT::Key`
   - `AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>::registerPass()` at line 471-485: stores analysis in `AnalysisPasses` map keyed by `PassT::ID()`

2. **PassManager::run()** - `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerImpl.h` (line 28)
   - Iterates `Passes` vector, calls `Pass->run(IR, AM, ExtraArgs...)` on each
   - After each pass: `AM.invalidate(IR, PassPA)` based on returned `PreservedAnalyses`
   - Calls `PI.runBeforePass` / `PI.runAfterPass` for instrumentation

3. **Type-erasure layer** - `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h`
   - `PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` - abstract base with virtual `run()`, `name()`, `isRequired()`
   - `PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` - concrete wrapper, `run()` delegates to `Pass.run(IR, AM, ExtraArgs...)`
   - `AnalysisResultConcept` / `AnalysisResultModel` - same pattern for analysis results

4. **Explicit instantiations** - `llvm/lib/IR/PassManager.cpp`
   - `template class PassManager<Module>` → `ModulePassManager`

## How a New LLVM Optimization Pass Is Registered and Executed

### 1. PassManager Template — `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`

**`PassInfoMixin<DerivedT>`** (line 70) is the CRTP base every new-PM transformation pass inherits from. It provides `static StringRef name()` (strips `llvm::` from the demangled type name) and `printPipeline()`.

**`AnalysisInfoMixin<DerivedT>`** (line 93) extends `PassInfoMixin` for analysis passes. It adds `static AnalysisKey* ID()` returning `&DerivedT::Key` — a static member that serves as the unique identity token for that analysis type.

**`PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>`** (line 159) is the core template:
```cpp
template <typename IRUnitT,
          typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,
          typename... ExtraArgTs>
class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<PassManager<...>> {
  std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;  // line 225
};
```
Convenience typedefs: `ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>` (line 238), `FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>` (line 247).

**Type-erasure layer** — `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h`:
- `PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` (line 40): abstract base with pure-virtual `run()`, `name()`, `isRequired()`, `printPipeline()`.
- `PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` (line 72): concrete wrapper holding a `PassT` by value. Its `run()` at line 89–92 simply calls `Pass.run(IR, AM, ExtraArgs...)`.

**Explicit instantiations** — `llvm/lib/IR/PassManager.cpp` (line 20–29): forces `PassManager<Module>`, `PassManager<Function>`, `AnalysisManager<Module>`, `AnalysisManager<Function>`,
... (truncated)

There\n    11  /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n    12  /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n    13  /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n    14  /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n    15  /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n    16  /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n    17  /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n    18  /// single module provided.\n    19  ///\n    20  /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n    21  /// modules and functions.\n    22  ///\n    23  /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n    24  ///   a Function.\n    25  /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n    26  ///\n    27  /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n    28  /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n    29  /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n    30  /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n    31  /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n    32  /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n    33  /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n    34  ///\n    35 56\n    57    // Now walk all the functions to see if any inner analysis invalidation is\n    58    // necessary.\n    59    for (Function &F : M) {\n    60      std::optional<PreservedAnalyses>   // registered with the outer analysis manager proxy for this function.\n    65      if (auto *OuterProxy =\n    66              InnerAM->getCachedResult<ModuleAnalysisManagerFunctionProxy>(F))\n    67        for (const auto &OuterInvalidationPair :\n    68             OuterProxy->getOuterInvalidations()) {\n    69          AnalysisKey *OuterAnalysisID = OuterInvalidationPair.first;\n    70 PA;\n    74            for (AnalysisKey *InnerAnalysisID : InnerAnalysisIDs)\n    75              FunctionPA->abandon(InnerAnalysisID);\n    76          }\n    77        }\n    78\n    79      // At application startup, passes are registered\n    11  // with the PassRegistry, which is later provided to the PassManager for\n    12  // dependency resolution and similar tasks.\n    13  //\n    14  //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    15\n    16  #ifndef LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n    17  #define LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n    18\n    19  #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n    20  #include \"llvm/ADT/StringMap.h\"\n    21  #include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n    22  #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n    23  #include \"llvm/Support/RWMutex.h\"\n    24  #include <memory>\n    25  #include <vector>\n    26\n    27  namespace llvm {\n    28\n    29  class PassInfo;\n    30  struct PassRegistrationListener;\n    31\n    32  /// PassRegistry - This class manages the registration and intitialization of\n    33  /// the pass subsystem as application startup, and assists the PassManager\n    34  /// in resolving pass dependencies.\n    35  /// NOTE: PassRegistry is NOT thread-safe. Required in order to use the pass with a PassManager.\n    70    LLVM_ABI void registerPass(const PassInfo &PI, bool ShouldFree = false);\n    71\n    72    /// enumerateWith - Enumerate the registered passes, calling the provided\n    73    /// PassRegistrationListener's passEnumerate() callback on each of them.\n    74    LLVM_ABI void enumerateWith(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n    75\n    76    /// addRegistrationListener - Register the given PassRegistrationListener\n    77    /// to receive passRegistered() callbacks whenever a new pass is registered.\n    78    LLVM_ABI void addRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n    79\n    80    /// removeRegistrationListener - Unregister a PassRegistrationListener so that\n    81    /// it no longer receives passRegistered() callbacks.\n    82    LLVM_ABI void removeRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n    83  };\n    84\n    85  } // end namespace llvm\n    86\n    87  #endif // LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H"

"1  //===-------- LLVM-provided High-Level Optimization levels -*- C++ -*------===//\n     2  //\n     3  // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n     4  // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n     5  // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n     6  //\n     7  //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n     8  /// \\file\n     9  ///\n    10  /// This header enumerates the LLVM-provided high-level optimization levels.\n    11  /// Each level has a specific goal and rationale.\n    12  ///\n    13  //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    14\n    15  #ifndef LLVM_PASSES_OPTIMIZATIONLEVEL_H\n    16  #define LLVM_PASSES_OPTIMIZATIONLEVEL_H\n    17\n    18  #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n    19  #include <assert.h>\n    20\n    21  namespace llvm {\n    22\n    23  class OptimizationLevel final {\n    24    unsigned SpeedLevel = 2;\n    25    unsigned SizeLevel = 0;\n    26    OptimizationLevel(unsigned SpeedLevel, unsigned SizeLevel)\n    27        : SpeedLevel(SpeedLevel), SizeLevel(SizeLevel) {\n    28      // Check that only valid combinations are passed.\n    29      assert(SpeedLevel <= 3 &&\n    30             \"Optimization level for speed should be 0, 1, 2, or 3\");\n    31      assert(SizeLevel <= 2 &&\n    32             \"Optimization level for size should be 0, 1, or 2\");\n    33      assert((SizeLevel == 0 || SpeedLevel == 2) &&\n    34             \"Optimize for size should be encoded with speedup level == 2\");\n    35    }\n    36\n    37  public:\n    38    OptimizationLevel() = default;\n    39    /// Disable as many optimizations as possible. This doesn't completely\n    40    /// disable the optimizer in all cases, for example always_inline functions\n    41    /// can be required to be inlined for correctness.\n    42    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O0;\n    43\n    44    /// Optimize quickly without destroying debuggability.\n    45    ///\n    46    /// This level is tuned to produce a result from the optimizer as quickly\n    47    /// as possible and to avoid destroying debuggability. This tends to result\n    48    /// in a very good development mode where the compiled code will be\n    49    /// immediately executed as part of testing. As a consequence, where\n    50    /// possible, we would like to produce efficient-to-execute code, but not\n    51    /// if it significantly slows down compilation or would prevent even basic\n    52    /// debugging of the resulting binary.\n    53    ///\n    54    /// As an example, complex loop transformations such as versioning,\n    55    /// vectorization, or fusion don't make sense here due to the degree to\n    56    /// which the executed code differs from the source code, and the compile\n    57    /// time cost.\n    58    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O1;\n    59    /// Optimize for fast execution as much as possible without triggering\n    60    /// significant incremental compile time or code size growth.\n    61    ///\n    62    /// The key idea is that optimizations at this level should \"pay for\n    63    /// themselves\". So if an optimization increases compile time by 5% or\n    64    /// increases code size by 5% for a particular benchmark, that benchmark\n    65    /// should also be one which sees a 5% runtime improvement. If the compile\n    66    /// time or code size penalties happen on average across a diverse range of\n    67    /// LLVM users' benchmarks, then the improvements should as well.\n    68    ///\n    69    /// And no matter what, the compile time needs to not grow superlinearly\n    70    /// with the size of input to LLVM so that users can control the runtime of\n    71    /// the optimizer in this mode.\n    72    ///\n    73    /// This is expected to be a good default optimization level for the vast\n    74    /// majority of users.\n    75    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O2;\n    76    /// Optimize for fast execution as much as possible.\n    77    ///\n    78    /// This mode is significantly more aggressive in trading off compile time\n    79    /// and code size to get execution time improvements. The core idea is that\n    80    /// this mode should include any optimization that helps execution time on\n    81    /// balance across a diverse collection of benchmarks, even if it increases\n    82    /// code size or compile time for some benchmarks without corresponding\n    83    /// improvements to execution time.\n    84    ///\n    85    /// Despite being willing to trade more compile time off to get improved\n    86    /// execution time, this mode still tries to avoid superlinear growth in\n    87    /// order to make even significantly slower compile times at least scale\n    88    /// reasonably. This does not preclude very substantial constant factor\n    89    /// costs though.\n    90    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O3;\n    91    /// Similar to \\c O2 but tries to optimize for small code size instead of\n    92    /// fast execution without triggering significant incremental execution\n    93    /// time slowdowns.\n    94    ///\n    95    /// The logic here is exactly the same as \\c O2, but with code size and\n    96    /// execution time metrics swapped.\n    97    ///\n    98    /// A consequence of the different core goal is that this should in general\n    99    /// produce substantially smaller executables that still run in\n   100    /// a reasonable amount of time.\n   101    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel Os;\n   102    /// A very specialized mode that will optimize for code size at any and all\n   103    /// costs.\n   104    ///\n   105    /// This is useful primarily when there are absolute size limitations and\n   106    /// any effort taken to reduce the size is worth it regardless of the\n   107    /// execution time impact. You should expect this level to produce rather\n   108    /// slow, but very small, code.\n   109    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel Oz;\n   110\n   111    bool isOptimizingForSpeed() const { return SizeLevel == 0 && SpeedLevel > 0; }\n   112\n   113    bool isOptimizingForSize() const { return SizeLevel > 0; }\n   114\n   115    bool operator==(const OptimizationLevel &Other) const {\n   116      return SizeLevel == Other.SizeLevel && SpeedLevel == Other.SpeedLevel;\n   117    }\n   118    bool operator!=(const OptimizationLevel &Other) const {\n   119      return SizeLevel != Other.SizeLevel || SpeedLevel != Other.SpeedLevel;\n   120    }\n   121\n   122    unsigned getSpeedupLevel() const { return SpeedLevel; }\n   123\n   124    unsigned getSizeLevel() const { return SizeLevel; }\n   125  };\n   126  } // namespace llvm\n   127\n   128  #endif"

"1  //===-------- LLVM-provided High-Level Optimization levels -*- C++ -*------===//\n     2  //\n     3  // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n     4  // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n     5  // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n     6  //\n     7  //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n     8  /// \\file\n     9  ///\n    10  /// This header enumerates the LLVM-provided high-level optimization levels.\n    11  /// Each level has a specific goal and rationale.\n    12  ///\n    13  //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    14\n    15  #ifndef LLVM_PASSES_OPTIMIZATIONLEVEL_H\n    16  #define LLVM_PASSES_OPTIMIZATIONLEVEL_H\n    17\n    18  #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n    19  #include <assert.h>\n    20\n    21  namespace llvm {\n    22\n    23  class OptimizationLevel final {\n    24    unsigned SpeedLevel = 2;\n    25    unsigned SizeLevel = 0;\n    26    OptimizationLevel(unsigned SpeedLevel, unsigned SizeLevel)\n    27        : SpeedLevel(SpeedLevel), SizeLevel(SizeLevel) {\n    28      // Check that only valid combinations are passed.\n    29      assert(SpeedLevel <= 3 &&\n    30             \"Optimization level for speed should be 0, 1, 2, or 3\");\n    31      assert(SizeLevel <= 2 &&\n    32             \"Optimization level for size should be 0, 1, or 2\");\n    33      assert((SizeLevel == 0 || SpeedLevel == 2) &&\n    34             \"Optimize for size should be encoded with speedup level == 2\");\n    35    }\n    36\n    37  public:\n    38    OptimizationLevel() = default;\n    39    /// Disable as many optimizations as possible. This doesn't completely\n    40    /// disable the optimizer in all cases, for example always_inline functions\n    41    /// can be required to be inlined for correctness.\n    42    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O0;\n    43\n    44    /// Optimize quickly without destroying debuggability.\n    45    ///\n    46    /// This level is tuned to produce a result from the optimizer as quickly\n    47    /// as possible and to avoid destroying debuggability. This tends to result\n    48    /// in a very good development mode where the compiled code will be\n    49    /// immediately executed as part of testing. As a consequence, where\n    50    /// possible, we would like to produce efficient-to-execute code, but not\n    51    /// if it significantly slows down compilation or would prevent even basic\n    52    /// debugging of the resulting binary.\n    53    ///\n    54    /// As an example, complex loop transformations such as versioning,\n    55    /// vectorization, or fusion don't make sense here due to the degree to\n    56    /// which the executed code differs from the source code, and the compile\n    57    /// time cost.\n    58    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O1;\n    59    /// Optimize for fast execution as much as possible without triggering\n    60    /// significant incremental compile time or code size growth.\n    61    ///\n    62    /// The key idea is that optimizations at this level should \"pay for\n    63    /// themselves\". So if an optimization increases compile time by 5% or\n    64    /// increases code size by 5% for a particular benchmark, that benchmark\n    65    /// should also be one which sees a 5% runtime improvement. If the compile\n    66    /// time or code size penalties happen on average across a diverse range of\n    67    /// LLVM users' benchmarks, then the improvements should as well.\n    68    ///\n    69    /// And no matter what, the compile time needs to not grow superlinearly\n    70    /// with the size of input to LLVM so that users can control the runtime of\n    71    /// the optimizer in this mode.\n    72    ///\n    73    /// This is expected to be a good default optimization level for the vast\n    74    /// majority of users.\n    75    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O2;\n    76    /// Optimize for fast execution as much as possible.\n    77    ///\n    78    /// This mode is significantly more aggressive in trading off compile time\n    79    /// and code size to get execution time improvements. The core idea is that\n    80    /// this mode should include any optimization that helps execution time on\n    81    /// balance across a diverse collection of benchmarks, even if it increases\n    82    /// code size or compile time for some benchmarks without corresponding\n    83    /// improvements to execution time.\n    84    ///\n    85    /// Despite being willing to trade more compile time off to get improved\n    86    /// execution time, this mode still tries to avoid superlinear growth in\n    87    /// order to make even significantly slower compile times at least scale\n    88    /// reasonably. This does not preclude very substantial constant factor\n    89    /// costs though.\n    90    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel O3;\n    91    /// Similar to \\c O2 but tries to optimize for small code size instead of\n    92    /// fast execution without triggering significant incremental execution\n    93    /// time slowdowns.\n    94    ///\n    95    /// The logic here is exactly the same as \\c O2, but with code size and\n    96    /// execution time metrics swapped.\n    97    ///\n    98    /// A consequence of the different core goal is that this should in general\n    99    /// produce substantially smaller executables that still run in\n   100    /// a reasonable amount of time.\n   101    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel Os;\n   102    /// A very specialized mode that will optimize for code size at any and all\n   103    /// costs.\n   104    ///\n   105    /// This is useful primarily when there are absolute size limitations and\n   106    /// any effort taken to reduce the size is worth it regardless of the\n   107    /// execution time impact. You should expect this level to produce rather\n   108    /// slow, but very small, code.\n   109    LLVM_ABI static const OptimizationLevel Oz;\n   110\n   111    bool isOptimizingForSpeed() const { return SizeLevel == 0 && SpeedLevel > 0; }\n   112\n   113    bool isOptimizingForSize() const { return SizeLevel > 0; }\n   114\n   115    bool operator==(const OptimizationLevel &Other) const {\n   116      return SizeLevel == Other.SizeLevel && SpeedLevel == Other.SpeedLevel;\n   117    }\n   118    bool operator!=(const OptimizationLevel &Other) const {\n   119      return SizeLevel != Other.SizeLevel || SpeedLevel != Other.SpeedLevel;\n   120    }\n   121\n   122    unsigned getSpeedupLevel() const { return SpeedLevel; }\n   123\n   124    unsigned getSizeLevel() const { return SizeLevel; }\n   125  };\n   126  } // namespace llvm\n   127\n   128  #endif"
